00001 subroutine bashforth_set ( norder, xtab, weight )
00002 !
00003 !*******************************************************************************
00004 !
00005 !! BASHFORTH_SET sets abscissas and weights for Adams-Bashforth quadrature.
00006 !
00007 !
00008 !  Definition:
00009 !
00010 !    Adams-Bashforth quadrature formulas are normally used in solving
00011 !    ordinary differential equations, and are not really suitable for
00012 !    general quadrature computations.  However, an Adams-Bashforth formula
00013 !    is equivalent to approximating the integral of F(Y(X)) between X(M)
00014 !    and X(M+1), using an explicit formula that relies only on known values
00015 !    of F(Y(X)) at X(M-N+1) through X(M).  For this reason, the formulas
00016 !    have been included here.
00017 !
00018 !    Suppose the unknown function is denoted by Y(X), with derivative
00019 !    F(Y(X)), and that approximate values of the function are known at a
00020 !    series of X values, which we write as X(1), X(2), ..., X(M).  We write
00021 !    the value Y(X(1)) as Y(1) and so on.
00022 !
00023 !    Then the solution of the ODE Y'=F(X,Y) at the next point X(M+1) is
00024 !    computed by:
00025 !
00026 !      Y(M+1) = Y(M) + Integral ( X(M) < X < X(M+1) ) F(Y(X)) dX
00027 !             = Y(M) + H * Sum ( 1 <= I <= N ) W(I) * F(Y(M+1-I)) approximately.
00028 !
00029 !    In the documentation that follows, we replace F(Y(X)) by F(X).
00030 !
00031 !  Integration interval:
00032 !
00033 !    [ 0, 1 ].
00034 !
00035 !  Weight function:
00036 !
00037 !    1.0D+00
00038 !
00039 !  Integral to approximate:
00040 !
00041 !    Integral ( 0 <= X <= 1 ) F(X) dX.
00042 !
00043 !  Approximate integral:
00044 !
00045 !    Sum ( 1 <= I <= NORDER ) WEIGHT(I) * F ( 1 - I ),
00046 !
00047 !  Note:
00048 !
00049 !    The Adams-Bashforth formulas require equally spaced data.
00050 !
00051 !    Here is how the formula is applied in the case with non-unit spacing:
00052 !
00053 !      Integral ( A <= X <= A+H ) F(X) dX =
00054 !      H * Sum ( 1 <= I <= NORDER ) WEIGHT(I) * F ( A - (I-1)*H ),
00055 !      approximately.
00056 !
00057 !    The reference lists the second coefficient of the order 8 Adams-Bashforth
00058 !    formula as
00059 !      weight(2) =  -1162169.0D+00 / 120960.0D+00
00060 !    but this should be
00061 !      weight(2) =  -1152169.0D+00 / 120960.0D+00
00062 !
00063 !  Reference:
00064 !
00065 !    Abramowitz and Stegun,
00066 !    Handbook of Mathematical Functions,
00067 !    National Bureau of Standards, 1964.
00068 !
00069 !    Jean Lapidus and John Seinfeld,
00070 !    Numerical Solution of Ordinary Differential Equations,
00071 !    Academic Press, 1971.
00072 !
00073 !    Daniel Zwillinger, editor,
00074 !    Standard Mathematical Tables and Formulae,
00075 !    30th Edition,
00076 !    CRC Press, 1996.
00077 !
00078 !  Modified:
00079 !
00080 !    15 September 1998
00081 !
00082 !  Author:
00083 !
00084 !    John Burkardt
00085 !
00086 !  Parameters:
00087 !
00088 !    Input, integer NORDER, the order of the rule.  NORDER should be
00089 !    between 1 and 8.
00090 !
00091 !    Output, double precision XTAB(NORDER), the abscissas of the rule.
00092 !
00093 !    Output, double precision WEIGHT(NORDER), the weights of the rule.
00094 !    WEIGHT(1) is the weight at X = 0, WEIGHT(2) the weight at X = -1,
00095 !    and so on.  The weights are rational, and should sum to 1.  Some
00096 !    weights may be negative.
00097 !
00098   implicit none
00099 !
00100   integer norder
00101 !
00102   double precision d
00103   integer i
00104   double precision weight(norder)
00105   double precision xtab(norder)
00106 !
00107   if ( norder == 1 ) then
00108 
00109     weight(1) = 1.0D+00
00110 
00111   else if ( norder == 2 ) then
00112 
00113     d = 2.0D+00
00114 
00115     weight(1) =   3.0D+00 / d
00116     weight(2) = - 1.0D+00 / d
00117 
00118   else if ( norder == 3 ) then
00119 
00120     d = 12.0D+00
00121 
00122     weight(1) =   23.0D+00 / d
00123     weight(2) = - 16.0D+00 / d
00124     weight(3) =    5.0D+00 / d
00125 
00126   else if ( norder == 4 ) then
00127 
00128     d = 24.0D+00
00129 
00130     weight(1) =   55.0D+00 / d
00131     weight(2) = - 59.0D+00 / d
00132     weight(3) =   37.0D+00 / d
00133     weight(4) =  - 9.0D+00 / d
00134 
00135   else if ( norder == 5 ) then
00136 
00137     d = 720.0D+00
00138 
00139     weight(1) =   1901.0D+00 / d
00140     weight(2) = - 2774.0D+00 / d
00141     weight(3) =   2616.0D+00 / d
00142     weight(4) = - 1274.0D+00 / d
00143     weight(5) =    251.0D+00 / d
00144 
00145   else if ( norder == 6 ) then
00146 
00147     d = 1440.0D+00
00148 
00149     weight(1) =   4277.0D+00 / d
00150     weight(2) = - 7923.0D+00 / d
00151     weight(3) =   9982.0D+00 / d
00152     weight(4) = - 7298.0D+00 / d
00153     weight(5) =   2877.0D+00 / d
00154     weight(6) =  - 475.0D+00 / d
00155 
00156   else if ( norder == 7 ) then
00157 
00158     d = 60480.0D+00
00159 
00160     weight(1) =    198721.0D+00 / d
00161     weight(2) =  - 447288.0D+00 / d
00162     weight(3) =    705549.0D+00 / d
00163     weight(4) =  - 688256.0D+00 / d
00164     weight(5) =    407139.0D+00 / d
00165     weight(6) =  - 134472.0D+00 / d
00166     weight(7) =     19087.0D+00 / d
00167 
00168   else if ( norder == 8 ) then
00169 
00170     d = 120960.0D+00
00171 
00172     weight(1) =     434241.0D+00 / d
00173     weight(2) =  - 1152169.0D+00 / d
00174     weight(3) =    2183877.0D+00 / d
00175     weight(4) =  - 2664477.0D+00 / d
00176     weight(5) =    2102243.0D+00 / d
00177     weight(6) =  - 1041723.0D+00 / d
00178     weight(7) =     295767.0D+00 / d
00179     weight(8) =    - 36799.0D+00 / d
00180 
00181   else
00182 
00183     write ( *, '(a)' ) ' '
00184     write ( *, '(a)' ) 'BASHFORTH_SET - Fatal error!'
00185     write ( *, '(a,i6)' ) '  Illegal value of NORDER = ', norder
00186     write ( *, '(a)' ) '  Legal values are 1 through 8.'
00187     stop
00188 
00189   end if
00190 
00191   do i = 1, norder
00192     xtab(i) = dble ( 1 - i )
00193   end do
00194 
00195   return
00196 end
00197 subroutine bdf_set ( norder, alpha, beta, gamma )
00198 !
00199 !*******************************************************************************
00200 !
00201 !! BDF_SET sets weights for backward differentiation ODE weights.
00202 !
00203 !
00204 !  Discussion:
00205 !
00206 !    GAMMA * Y(N+1) = Sum ( 1 <= I <= NORDER ) ALPHA(I) * Y(N+1-I)
00207 !                     + dX * BETA * Y'(X(N+1),Y(N+1))
00208 !
00209 !    This is equivalent to the backward differentiation corrector formulas.
00210 !
00211 !  Modified:
00212 !
00213 !    30 December 1999
00214 !
00215 !  Author:
00216 !
00217 !    John Burkardt
00218 !
00219 !  Parameters:
00220 !
00221 !    Input, integer NORDER, the order of the rule, between 1 and 6.
00222 !
00223 !    Output, double precision ALPHA(NORDER), BETA, GAMMA, the weights.
00224 !
00225   implicit none
00226 !
00227   integer norder
00228 !
00229   double precision alpha(norder)
00230   double precision beta
00231   double precision gamma
00232 !
00233   if ( norder == 1 ) then
00234     beta =     1.0D+00
00235     gamma =    1.0D+00
00236     alpha(1) = 1.0D+00
00237   else if ( norder == 2 ) then
00238     beta =       2.0D+00
00239     gamma =      3.0D+00
00240     alpha(1) =   4.0D+00
00241     alpha(2) = - 1.0D+00
00242   else if ( norder == 3 ) then
00243     beta =       6.0D+00
00244     gamma =     11.0D+00
00245     alpha(1) =  18.0D+00
00246     alpha(2) = - 9.0D+00
00247     alpha(3) =   2.0D+00
00248   else if ( norder == 4 ) then
00249     beta =       12.0D+00
00250     gamma =      25.0D+00
00251     alpha(1) =   48.0D+00
00252     alpha(2) = - 36.0D+00
00253     alpha(3) =   16.0D+00
00254     alpha(4) =  - 3.0D+00
00255   else if ( norder == 5 ) then
00256     beta =        60.0D+00
00257     gamma =      137.0D+00
00258     alpha(1) =   300.0D+00
00259     alpha(2) = - 300.0D+00
00260     alpha(3) =   200.0D+00
00261     alpha(4) =  - 75.0D+00
00262     alpha(5) =    12.0D+00
00263   else if ( norder == 6 ) then
00264     beta =        60.0D+00
00265     gamma =      147.0D+00
00266     alpha(1) =   360.0D+00
00267     alpha(2) = - 450.0D+00
00268     alpha(3) =   400.0D+00
00269     alpha(4) = - 225.0D+00
00270     alpha(5) =    72.0D+00
00271     alpha(6) =  - 10.0D+00
00272   else
00273     write ( *, '(a)' ) ' '
00274     write ( *, '(a)' ) 'BDF_SET - Fatal error!'
00275     write ( *, '(a,i6)' ) '  Illegal order requested = ', norder
00276     stop
00277   end if
00278 
00279   return
00280 end
00281 subroutine bdfc_set ( norder, weight, xtab )
00282 !
00283 !*******************************************************************************
00284 !
00285 !! BDFC_SET sets weights for backward differentiation corrector quadrature.
00286 !
00287 !
00288 !  Definition:
00289 !
00290 !    A backward differentiation corrector formula is defined for a set
00291 !    of evenly spaced abscissas X(I) with X(1) = 1 and X(2) = 0.  Assuming
00292 !    that the values of the function to be integrated are known at the
00293 !    abscissas, the formula is written in terms of the function value at
00294 !    X(1), and the backward differences at X(1) that approximate the
00295 !    derivatives there.
00296 !
00297 !  Integration interval:
00298 !
00299 !    [ 0, 1 ]
00300 !
00301 !  Weight function:
00302 !
00303 !    1.0D+00
00304 !
00305 !  Integral to approximate:
00306 !
00307 !    Integral ( 0 <= X <= 1 ) F(X) dX
00308 !
00309 !  Approximate integral:
00310 !
00311 !    Sum ( 1 <= I <= NORDER ) WEIGHT(I) * BD**(I-1) F ( 1 ).
00312 !
00313 !    Here, "BD**(I-1) F ( 1 )" denotes the (I-1)st backward difference
00314 !    of F at X = 1, using a spacing of 1.  In particular,
00315 !
00316 !    BD**0 F(1) = F(1)
00317 !    BD**1 F(1) = F(1) - F(0)
00318 !    BD**2 F(1) = F(1) - 2 * F(0) + F(-1 )
00319 !
00320 !  Note:
00321 !
00322 !    The relationship between a backward difference corrector and the
00323 !    corresponding Adams-Moulton formula may be illustrated for the
00324 !    BDF corrector of order 4:
00325 !
00326 !      BD**0 F(1) - 1/2 * BD**1 F(1) - 1/12 * BD**2 F(1) - 1/24 * BDF**3 F(1)
00327 !      =            F(1)
00328 !        -  1/2 * ( F(1) -         F(0) )
00329 !        - 1/12 * ( F(1) - 2     * F(0) +        F(-1) )
00330 !        - 1/24 * ( F(1) - 3     * F(0) + 3    * F(-1) -        F(-2) )
00331 !      =   9/24 *   F(1) + 19/24 * F(0) - 5/24 * F(-1) + 1/24 * F(-2)
00332 !
00333 !    which is the Adams-Moulton formula of order 4.
00334 ! 
00335 !  Reference:
00336 !
00337 !    Simeon Fatunla,
00338 !    Numerical Methods for Initial Value Problems in Ordinary Differential
00339 !      Equations,
00340 !    Academic Press, 1988.
00341 !
00342 !  Modified:
00343 !
00344 !    28 February 2000
00345 !
00346 !  Author:
00347 !
00348 !    John Burkardt
00349 !
00350 !  Parameters:
00351 !
00352 !    Input, integer NORDER, the order of the rule, which can be
00353 !    any value from 1 to 19.
00354 !
00355 !    Output, double precision WEIGHT(NORDER), the weights of the rule.
00356 !
00357 !    Output, double precision XTAB(NORDER), the abscissas of the rule.
00358 !
00359   implicit none
00360 !
00361   integer, parameter :: maxord = 19
00362 !
00363   integer norder
00364 !
00365   integer i
00366   double precision w(maxord)
00367   double precision weight(norder)
00368   double precision xtab(norder)
00369 !
00370   w(1) =                 1.0D+00
00371   w(2) =               - 1.0D+00 /               2.0D+00
00372   w(3) =               - 1.0D+00 /              12.0D+00
00373   w(4) =               - 1.0D+00 /              24.0D+00
00374   w(5) =              - 19.0D+00 /             720.0D+00
00375   w(6) =               - 3.0D+00 /             160.0D+00
00376   w(7) =             - 863.0D+00 /           60480.0D+00
00377   w(8) =             - 275.0D+00 /           24792.0D+00
00378   w(9) =           - 33953.0D+00 /         3628800.0D+00
00379   w(10) =           - 8183.0D+00 /         1036800.0D+00
00380   w(11) =        - 3250433.0D+00 /       479001600.0D+00
00381   w(12) =           - 4671.0D+00 /          788480.0D+00
00382   w(13) =    - 13695779093.0D+00 /   2615348736000.0D+00
00383   w(14) =     - 2224234463.0D+00 /    475517952000.0D+00
00384   w(15) =   - 132282840127.0D+00 /  31384184832000.0D+00
00385   w(16) =     - 2639651053.0D+00 /    689762304000.0D+00
00386   w(17) =  111956703448001.0D+00 /   3201186852864.0D+00
00387   w(18) =         50188465.0D+00 /     15613165568.0D+00
00388   w(19) = 2334028946344463.0D+00 / 786014494949376.0D+00
00389 
00390   do i = 1, min ( norder, maxord )
00391     weight(i) = w(i)
00392   end do
00393 
00394   do i = 1, norder
00395     xtab(i) = dble ( 2 - i )
00396   end do
00397 
00398   return
00399 end
00400 subroutine bdfp_set ( norder, weight, xtab )
00401 !
00402 !*******************************************************************************
00403 !
00404 !! BDFP_SET sets weights for backward differentiation predictor quadrature.
00405 !
00406 !
00407 !  Definition:
00408 !
00409 !    A backward differentiation predictor formula is defined for a set
00410 !    of evenly spaced abscissas X(I) with X(1) = 1 and X(2) = 0.  Assuming
00411 !    that the values of the function to be integrated are known at the
00412 !    abscissas, the formula is written in terms of the function value at
00413 !    X(2), and the backward differences at X(2) that approximate the
00414 !    derivatives there.  A backward differentiation predictor formula
00415 !    is equivalent to an Adams-Bashforth formula of the same order.
00416 !
00417 !  Integration interval:
00418 !
00419 !    [ 0, 1 ]
00420 !
00421 !  Weight function:
00422 !
00423 !    1.0D+00
00424 !
00425 !  Integral to approximate:
00426 !
00427 !    Integral ( 0 <= X <= 1 ) F(X) dX
00428 !
00429 !  Approximate integral:
00430 !
00431 !    Sum ( 1 <= I <= NORDER ) WEIGHT(I) * BD**(I-1) F ( 0 ),
00432 !
00433 !    Here, "BD**(I-1) F ( 0 )" denotes the (I-1)st backward difference
00434 !    of F at X = 0, using a spacing of 1.  In particular,
00435 !
00436 !    BD**0 F(0) = F(0)
00437 !    BD**1 F(0) = F(0) - F(-1)
00438 !    BD**2 F(0) = F(0) - 2 * F(-1) + F(-2 )
00439 !
00440 !  Note:
00441 !
00442 !    The relationship between a backward difference predictor and the
00443 !    corresponding Adams-Bashforth formula may be illustrated for the
00444 !    BDF predictor of order 3:
00445 !
00446 !      BD**0 F(0) + 0.5 * BD**1 F(0) + 5/12 * BD**2 F(0)
00447 !      =            F(0)
00448 !        + 1/2  * ( F(0) -         F(1) )
00449 !        + 5/12 * ( F(0) - 2     * F(-1) +      F(-2) )
00450 !      =  23/12 *   F(0) - 16/12 * F(-1) + 5/12 F(-2)
00451 !
00452 !    which is the Adams-Bashforth formula of order 3.
00453 ! 
00454 !  Reference:
00455 !
00456 !    Simeon Fatunla,
00457 !    Numerical Methods for Initial Value Problems in Ordinary Differential
00458 !      Equations,
00459 !    Academic Press, 1988.
00460 !
00461 !  Modified:
00462 !
00463 !    29 February 2000
00464 !
00465 !  Author:
00466 !
00467 !    John Burkardt
00468 !
00469 !  Parameters:
00470 !
00471 !    Input, integer NORDER, the order of the rule, which can be
00472 !    any value from 1 to 19.
00473 !
00474 !    Output, double precision WEIGHT(NORDER), the weight of the rule.
00475 !
00476 !    Output, double precision XTAB(NORDER), the abscissas of the rule.
00477 !
00478   implicit none
00479 !
00480   integer, parameter :: maxord = 19
00481 !
00482   integer norder
00483 !
00484   integer i
00485   double precision w(maxord)
00486   double precision weight(norder)
00487   double precision xtab(norder)
00488 !
00489   w(1) =                       1.0D+00
00490   w(2) =                       1.0D+00 /                2.0D+00
00491   w(3) =                       5.0D+00 /               12.0D+00
00492   w(4) =                       3.0D+00 /                8.0D+00
00493   w(5) =                     251.0D+00 /              720.0D+00
00494   w(6) =                      95.0D+00 /              288.0D+00
00495   w(7) =                   19087.0D+00 /            60480.0D+00
00496   w(8) =                    5257.0D+00 /            17280.0D+00
00497   w(9) =                 1070017.0D+00 /          3628800.0D+00
00498   w(10) =                  25713.0D+00 /            89600.0D+00
00499   w(11) =               26842253.0D+00 /         95800320.0D+00
00500   w(12) =                4777223.0D+00 /         17418240.0D+00
00501   w(13) =           703604254357.0D+00 /    2615348736000.0D+00
00502   w(14) =           106364763817.0D+00 /     402361344000.0D+00
00503   w(15) =          1166309819657.0D+00 /    4483454976000.0D+00
00504   w(16) =               25221445.0D+00 /         98402304.0D+00
00505   w(17) =       8092989203533249.0D+00 /    3201186852864.0D+00
00506   w(18) =         85455477715379.0D+00 /      34237292544.0D+00
00507   w(19) =   12600467236042756559.0D+00 / 5109094217170944.0D+00
00508 
00509   do i = 1, min ( norder, maxord )
00510     weight(i) = w(i)
00511   end do
00512 
00513   do i = 1, norder
00514     xtab(i) = dble ( 1 - i )
00515   end do
00516 
00517   return
00518 end
00519 subroutine bdf_sum ( func, norder, weight, xtab, diftab, result )
00520 !
00521 !*******************************************************************************
00522 !
00523 !! BDF_SUM carries out an explicit backward difference quadrature rule for [0,1].
00524 !
00525 !
00526 !  Integral to approximate:
00527 !
00528 !    Integral ( 0 <= X <= 1 ) F(X) dX
00529 !
00530 !  Formula:
00531 !
00532 !    RESULT = Sum ( 1 <= I <= NORDER ) WEIGHT(I) * BDF**(I-1) FUNC ( 0 )
00533 !
00534 !  Note:
00535 !
00536 !    The integral from 0 to 1 is approximated using data at X = 0,
00537 !    -1, -2, ..., -NORDER+1.  This is a form of extrapolation, and
00538 !    the approximation can become poor as NORDER increases.
00539 !
00540 !  Modified:
00541 !
00542 !    26 October 2000
00543 !
00544 !  Author:
00545 !
00546 !    John Burkardt
00547 !
00548 !  Parameters:
00549 !
00550 !    Input, external FUNC, the name of the FORTRAN function which evaluates
00551 !    the integrand.  The function must have the form
00552 !      double precision func ( x ).
00553 !
00554 !    Input, integer NORDER, the order of the rule.
00555 !
00556 !    Input, double precision WEIGHT(NORDER), the weights of the rule.
00557 !
00558 !    Input, double precision XTAB(NORDER), the abscissas of the rule.
00559 !
00560 !    Workspace, double precision DIFTAB(NORDER).
00561 !
00562 !    Output, double precision RESULT, the approximate value of the integral.
00563 !
00564   implicit none
00565 !
00566   integer norder
00567 !
00568   double precision diftab(norder)
00569   double precision, external :: func
00570   integer i
00571   integer j
00572   double precision result
00573   double precision weight(norder)
00574   double precision xtab(norder)
00575 !
00576   do i = 1, norder
00577     diftab(i) = func ( xtab(i) )
00578   end do
00579 
00580   do i = 2, norder
00581     do j = i, norder
00582       diftab(norder+i-j) = ( diftab(norder+i-j-1) - diftab(norder+i-j) )
00583     end do
00584   end do
00585 
00586   result = dot_product ( weight(1:norder), diftab(1:norder) )
00587 
00588   return
00589 end
00590 subroutine cheb_set ( norder, xtab, weight )
00591 !
00592 !*******************************************************************************
00593 !
00594 !! CHEB_SET sets abscissas and weights for Chebyshev quadrature.
00595 !
00596 !
00597 !  Integration interval:
00598 !
00599 !    [ -1, 1 ]
00600 !
00601 !  Weight function:
00602 !
00603 !    1.0D+00
00604 !
00605 !  Integral to approximate:
00606 !
00607 !    Integral ( -1 <= X <= 1 ) F(X) dX
00608 !
00609 !  Approximate integral:
00610 !
00611 !    Sum ( 1 <= I <= NORDER ) WEIGHT(I) * F ( XTAB(I) )
00612 !
00613 !  Note:
00614 !
00615 !    The Chebyshev rule is distinguished by using equal weights.
00616 !
00617 !  Reference:
00618 !
00619 !    Abramowitz and Stegun,
00620 !    Handbook of Mathematical Functions,
00621 !    National Bureau of Standards, 1964.
00622 !
00623 !    H Engels,
00624 !    Numerical Quadrature and Cubature,
00625 !    Academic Press, 1980.
00626 !
00627 !    Zdenek Kopal,
00628 !    Numerical Analysis,
00629 !    John Wiley, 1955.
00630 !
00631 !    Daniel Zwillinger, editor,
00632 !    Standard Mathematical Tables and Formulae,
00633 !    30th Edition,
00634 !    CRC Press, 1996.
00635 !
00636 !  Modified:
00637 !
00638 !    27 October 2000
00639 !
00640 !  Author:
00641 !
00642 !    John Burkardt
00643 !
00644 !  Parameters:
00645 !
00646 !    Input, integer NORDER, the order of the rule.
00647 !    NORDER may only have the values 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 7 or 9.
00648 !    There are NO other Chebyshev rules with real abscissas.
00649 !
00650 !    Output, double precision XTAB(NORDER), the abscissas of the rule,
00651 !    which are symmetric in [-1,1].
00652 !
00653 !    Output, double precision WEIGHT(NORDER), the weights of the rule,
00654 !    which should each equal 2 / NORDER.
00655 !
00656   implicit none
00657 !
00658   integer norder
00659 !
00660   integer i
00661   double precision weight(norder)
00662   double precision xtab(norder)
00663 !
00664   if ( norder == 1 ) then
00665 
00666     xtab(1) = 0.0D+00
00667 
00668   else if ( norder == 2 ) then
00669 
00670     xtab(1) = - 1.0D+00 / sqrt ( 3.0D+00 )
00671     xtab(2) =   1.0D+00 / sqrt ( 3.0D+00 )
00672 
00673   else if ( norder == 3 ) then
00674 
00675     xtab(1) = - 1.0D+00 / sqrt ( 2.0D+00 )
00676     xtab(2) =   0.0D+00
00677     xtab(3) =   1.0D+00 / sqrt ( 2.0D+00 )
00678 
00679   else if ( norder == 4 ) then
00680 
00681     xtab(1) =   - sqrt ( ( 1.0D+00 + 2.0D+00/ sqrt ( 5.0D+00 ) ) / 3.0D+00 )
00682     xtab(2) =   - sqrt ( ( 1.0D+00 - 2.0D+00/ sqrt ( 5.0D+00 ) ) / 3.0D+00 )
00683     xtab(3) =     sqrt ( ( 1.0D+00 - 2.0D+00/ sqrt ( 5.0D+00 ) ) / 3.0D+00 )
00684     xtab(4) =     sqrt ( ( 1.0D+00 + 2.0D+00/ sqrt ( 5.0D+00 ) ) / 3.0D+00 )
00685 
00686   else if ( norder == 5 ) then
00687 
00688     xtab(1) = - sqrt ( ( 5.0D+00 + sqrt ( 11.0D+00) ) / 12.0D+00 )
00689     xtab(2) = - sqrt ( ( 5.0D+00 - sqrt ( 11.0D+00) ) / 12.0D+00 )
00690     xtab(3) =   0.0D+00
00691     xtab(4) =   sqrt ( ( 5.0D+00 - sqrt ( 11.0D+00) ) / 12.0D+00 )
00692     xtab(5) =   sqrt ( ( 5.0D+00 + sqrt ( 11.0D+00) ) / 12.0D+00 )
00693 
00694   else if ( norder == 6 ) then
00695 
00696     xtab(1) = - 0.866246818107820591383598D+00
00697     xtab(2) = - 0.422518653761111529118546D+00
00698     xtab(3) = - 0.266635401516704720331534D+00
00699     xtab(4) =   0.266635401516704720331534D+00
00700     xtab(5) =   0.422518653761111529118546D+00
00701     xtab(6) =   0.866246818107820591383598D+00
00702 
00703   else if ( norder == 7 ) then
00704 
00705     xtab(1) = - 0.883861700758049035704224D+00
00706     xtab(2) = - 0.529656775285156811385048D+00
00707     xtab(3) = - 0.323911810519907637519673D+00
00708     xtab(4) =   0.0D+00
00709     xtab(5) =   0.323911810519907637519673D+00
00710     xtab(6) =   0.529656775285156811385048D+00
00711     xtab(7) =   0.883861700758049035704224D+00
00712 
00713   else if ( norder == 9 ) then
00714 
00715     xtab(1) = - 0.911589307728434473664949D+00
00716     xtab(2) = - 0.601018655380238071428128D+00
00717     xtab(3) = - 0.528761783057879993260181D+00
00718     xtab(4) = - 0.167906184214803943068031D+00
00719     xtab(5) =   0.0D+00
00720     xtab(6) =   0.167906184214803943068031D+00
00721     xtab(7) =   0.528761783057879993260181D+00
00722     xtab(8) =   0.601018655380238071428128D+00
00723     xtab(9) =   0.911589307728434473664949D+00
00724 
00725   else
00726 
00727     write ( *, '(a)' ) ' '
00728     write ( *, '(a)' ) 'CHEB_SET - Fatal error!'
00729     write ( *, '(a,i6)' ) '  Illegal value of NORDER = ', norder
00730     write ( *, '(a)' ) '  Legal values are 1 through 7, and 9.'
00731     stop
00732 
00733   end if
00734 
00735   weight(1:norder) = 2.0D+00 / dble ( norder )
00736 
00737   return
00738 end
00739 subroutine cheb_to_set ( norder, xtab, weight )
00740 !
00741 !*******************************************************************************
00742 !
00743 !! CHEB_TO_SET sets up open Gauss-Chebyshev (first kind) quadrature.
00744 !
00745 !
00746 !  Integration interval:
00747 !
00748 !    [ -1, 1 ]
00749 !
00750 !  Weight function:
00751 !
00752 !    1 / SQRT ( 1 - X**2 )
00753 !
00754 !  Integral to approximate:
00755 !
00756 !    Integral ( -1 <= X <= 1 ) F(X) / SQRT ( 1 - X**2 ) dX
00757 !
00758 !  Approximate integral:
00759 !
00760 !    Sum ( 1 <= I <= NORDER ) WEIGHT(I) * F ( XTAB(I) )
00761 !
00762 !  Precision:
00763 !
00764 !    If NORDER points are used, then Gauss-Chebyshev quadrature
00765 !    will compute the integral exactly, whenever F(X) is a polynomial
00766 !    of degree 2*NORDER-1 or less.
00767 !
00768 !  Note:
00769 !
00770 !    The abscissas of the rule are zeroes of the Chebyshev polynomials
00771 !    of the first kind, T(NORDER)(X).
00772 !
00773 !  Reference:
00774 !
00775 !    Daniel Zwillinger, editor,
00776 !    Standard Mathematical Tables and Formulae,
00777 !    30th Edition,
00778 !    CRC Press, 1996.
00779 !
00780 !  Modified:
00781 !
00782 !    15 September 1998
00783 !
00784 !  Author:
00785 !
00786 !    John Burkardt
00787 !
00788 !  Parameters:
00789 !
00790 !    Input, integer NORDER, the order of the rule.
00791 !
00792 !    Output, double precision XTAB(NORDER), the abscissas of the rule.
00793 !
00794 !    Output, double precision WEIGHT(NORDER), the weights of the rule,
00795 !    which are all equal to PI / NORDER.
00796 !
00797   implicit none
00798 !
00799   integer norder
00800 !
00801   double precision angle
00802   double precision d_pi
00803   integer i
00804   double precision weight(norder)
00805   double precision xtab(norder)
00806 !
00807   do i = 1, norder
00808     angle = dble ( 2 * i - 1 ) * d_pi ( ) / dble ( 2 * norder )
00809     xtab(i) = cos ( angle )
00810   end do
00811 
00812   weight(1:norder) = d_pi ( ) / dble ( norder )
00813 
00814   return
00815 end
00816 subroutine cheb_tc_set ( norder, xtab, weight )
00817 !
00818 !*******************************************************************************
00819 !
00820 !! CHEB_TC_SET sets up closed Gauss-Chebyshev (first kind) quadrature.
00821 !
00822 !
00823 !  Integration interval:
00824 !
00825 !    [ -1, 1 ]
00826 !
00827 !  Weight function:
00828 !
00829 !    1 / SQRT ( 1 - X**2 )
00830 !
00831 !  Integral to approximate:
00832 !
00833 !    Integral ( -1 <= X <= 1 ) F(X) / SQRT ( 1 - X**2 ) dX
00834 !
00835 !  Approximate integral:
00836 !
00837 !    Sum ( 1 <= I <= NORDER ) WEIGHT(I) * F ( XTAB(I) )
00838 !
00839 !  Precision:
00840 !
00841 !    If NORDER points are used, then Gauss-Chebyshev quadrature
00842 !    will compute the integral exactly, whenever F(X) is a polynomial
00843 !    of degree 2*NORDER-3 or less.
00844 !
00845 !  Note:
00846 !
00847 !    The abscissas include -1 and 1.
00848 !
00849 !    If the order is doubled, the abscissas of the new rule include
00850 !    all the points of the old rule.  This fact can be used to
00851 !    efficiently implement error estimation.
00852 !
00853 !  Reference:
00854 !
00855 !    Daniel Zwillinger, editor,
00856 !    Standard Mathematical Tables and Formulae,
00857 !    30th Edition,
00858 !    CRC Press, 1996.
00859 !
00860 !  Modified:
00861 !
00862 !    15 September 1998
00863 !
00864 !  Author:
00865 !
00866 !    John Burkardt
00867 !
00868 !  Parameters:
00869 !
00870 !    Input, integer NORDER, the order of the rule, which must be at least 2.
00871 !
00872 !    Output, double precision XTAB(NORDER), the abscissas of the rule.
00873 !
00874 !    Output, double precision WEIGHT(NORDER), the weights of the rule.
00875 !    The first and last weights are 0.5 * PI / ( NORDER - 1),
00876 !    and all other weights are PI / ( NORDER - 1 ).
00877 !
00878   implicit none
00879 !
00880   integer norder
00881 !
00882   double precision angle
00883   double precision d_pi
00884   integer i
00885   double precision weight(norder)
00886   double precision xtab(norder)
00887 !
00888   if ( norder < 2 ) then
00889     write ( *, '(a)' ) ' '
00890     write ( *, '(a)' ) 'CHEB_TC_SET - Fatal error!'
00891     write ( *, '(a)' ) '  NORDER must be at least 2.'
00892     write ( *, '(a,i6)' ) '  The input value was NORDER = ', norder
00893     stop
00894   end if
00895 
00896   do i = 1, norder
00897 
00898     angle = dble ( i - 1 ) * d_pi ( ) / dble ( norder - 1 )
00899     xtab(i) = cos ( angle )
00900 
00901   end do
00902 
00903   weight(1) = d_pi ( ) / dble ( 2 * ( norder - 1 ) )
00904   weight(2:norder-1) = d_pi ( ) / dble ( norder - 1 )
00905   weight(norder) = d_pi ( ) / dble ( 2 * ( norder - 1 ) )
00906 
00907   return
00908 end
00909 subroutine cheb_u_set ( norder, xtab, weight )
00910 !
00911 !*******************************************************************************
00912 !
00913 !! CHEB_U_SET sets abscissas and weights for Gauss-Chebyshev quadrature.
00914 !
00915 !
00916 !  Integration interval:
00917 !
00918 !    [ -1, 1 ]
00919 !
00920 !  Weight function:
00921 !
00922 !    SQRT ( 1 - X**2 )
00923 !
00924 !  Integral to approximate:
00925 !
00926 !    Integral ( -1 <= X <= 1 ) SQRT ( 1 - X**2 ) * F(X) dX
00927 !
00928 !  Approximate integral:
00929 !
00930 !    Sum ( 1 <= I <= NORDER ) WEIGHT(I) * F ( XTAB(I) )
00931 !
00932 !  Precision:
00933 !
00934 !    If NORDER points are used, then Gauss-Chebyshev quadrature
00935 !    will compute the integral exactly, whenever F(X) is a polynomial
00936 !    of degree 2*NORDER-1 or less.
00937 !
00938 !  Note:
00939 !
00940 !    The abscissas are zeroes of the Chebyshev polynomials
00941 !    of the second kind, U(NORDER)(X).
00942 !
00943 !  Reference:
00944 !
00945 !    Daniel Zwillinger, editor,
00946 !    Standard Mathematical Tables and Formulae,
00947 !    30th Edition,
00948 !    CRC Press, 1996.
00949 !
00950 !  Modified:
00951 !
00952 !    15 September 1998
00953 !
00954 !  Author:
00955 !
00956 !    John Burkardt
00957 !
00958 !  Parameters:
00959 !
00960 !    Input, integer NORDER, the order of the rule.
00961 !
00962 !    Output, double precision XTAB(NORDER), the abscissas of the rule.
00963 !
00964 !    Output, double precision WEIGHT(NORDER), the weights of the rule,
00965 !    which are all equal to PI / NORDER.
00966 !
00967   implicit none
00968 !
00969   integer norder
00970 !
00971   double precision angle
00972   double precision d_pi
00973   integer i
00974   double precision weight(norder)
00975   double precision xtab(norder)
00976 !
00977   do i = 1, norder
00978     angle = dble ( i ) * d_pi ( ) / dble ( norder + 1 )
00979     xtab(i) = cos ( angle )
00980     weight(i) = d_pi ( ) * ( sin ( angle ) )**2 / dble ( norder + 1 )
00981   end do
00982 
00983   return
00984 end
00985 subroutine d_swap ( x, y )
00986 !
00987 !*******************************************************************************
00988 !
00989 !! D_SWAP switches two double precision values.
00990 !
00991 !
00992 !  Modified:
00993 !
00994 !    01 May 2000
00995 !
00996 !  Author:
00997 !
00998 !    John Burkardt
00999 !
01000 !  Parameters:
01001 !
01002 !    Input/output, double precision X, Y.  On output, the values of X and
01003 !    Y have been interchanged.
01004 !
01005   implicit none
01006 !
01007   double precision x
01008   double precision y
01009   double precision z
01010 !
01011   z = x
01012   x = y
01013   y = z
01014 
01015   return
01016 end
01017 function d_pi ( )
01018 !
01019 !*******************************************************************************
01020 !
01021 !! DPI returns the value of pi as a double precision quantity.
01022 !
01023 !
01024 !  Modified:
01025 !
01026 !    28 April 2000
01027 !
01028 !  Author:
01029 !
01030 !    John Burkardt
01031 !
01032 !  Parameters:
01033 !
01034 !    Output, double precision D_PI, the value of pi.
01035 !
01036   implicit none
01037 !
01038   double precision d_pi
01039 !
01040   d_pi = 3.14159265358979323846264338327950288419716939937510D+00
01041 
01042   return
01043 end
01044 subroutine dvec_reverse ( n, a )
01045 !
01046 !*******************************************************************************
01047 !
01048 !! DVEC_REVERSE reverses the elements of a double precision vector.
01049 !
01050 !
01051 !  Example:
01052 !
01053 !    Input:
01054 !
01055 !      N = 5, A = ( 11.0, 12.0, 13.0, 14.0, 15.0D+00 )
01056 !
01057 !    Output:
01058 !
01059 !      A = ( 15.0, 14.0, 13.0, 12.0, 11.0D+00 )
01060 !
01061 !  Modified:
01062 !
01063 !    06 October 1998
01064 !
01065 !  Author:
01066 !
01067 !    John Burkardt
01068 !
01069 !  Parameters:
01070 !
01071 !    Input, integer N, the number of entries in the array.
01072 !
01073 !    Input/output, double precision A(N), the array to be reversed.
01074 !
01075   implicit none
01076 !
01077   integer n
01078 !
01079   double precision a(n)
01080   integer i
01081 !
01082   do i = 1, n/2
01083     call d_swap ( a(i), a(n+1-i) )
01084   end do
01085 
01086   return
01087 end
01088 function gamma ( x )
01089 !
01090 !*******************************************************************************
01091 !
01092 !! GAMMA computes the gamma function using Hastings's approximation.
01093 !
01094 !
01095 !  Reference:
01096 !
01097 !    Arthur Stroud and Don Secrest,
01098 !    Gaussian Quadrature Formulas,
01099 !    Prentice Hall, 1966.
01100 !
01101 !  Modified:
01102 !
01103 !    19 September 1998
01104 !
01105 !  Parameters:
01106 !
01107 !    Input, double precision X, the argument at which the gamma function
01108 !    is to be evaluated.  X must be greater than 0, and less than 70.
01109 !
01110 !    Output, double precision GAMMA, the gamma function at X.
01111 !
01112   implicit none
01113 !
01114   double precision gam
01115   double precision gamma
01116   double precision x
01117   double precision y
01118   double precision z
01119   double precision za
01120 !
01121   gam ( y ) = ((((((( &
01122           0.035868343D+00   * y &
01123         - 0.193527818D+00 ) * y &
01124         + 0.482199394D+00 ) * y &
01125         - 0.756704078D+00 ) * y &
01126         + 0.918206857D+00 ) * y &
01127         - 0.897056937D+00 ) * y &
01128         + 0.988205891D+00 ) * y &
01129         - 0.577191652D+00 ) * y + 1.0D+00
01130 
01131   if ( x <= 0.0D+00 ) then
01132     gamma = 0.0D+00
01133     write ( *, '(a)' ) ' '
01134     write ( *, '(a)' ) 'GAMMA - Fatal error!'
01135     write ( *, '(a)' ) '  Input argument X <= 0.'
01136     stop
01137   end if
01138 
01139   if ( x >= 70.0D+00 ) then
01140     write ( *, '(a)' ) ' '
01141     write ( *, '(a)' ) 'GAMMA - Fatal error!'
01142     write ( *, '(a)' ) '  Input argument X >= 70.'
01143     stop
01144   end if
01145 
01146   if ( x == 1.0D+00 ) then
01147     gamma = 1.0D+00
01148     return
01149   end if
01150 
01151   if ( x <= 1.0D+00 ) then
01152     gamma = gam ( x ) / x
01153     return
01154   end if
01155 
01156   z = x
01157 
01158   za = 1.0D+00
01159 
01160   do
01161 
01162     z = z - 1.0D+00
01163 
01164     if ( z < 1.0D+00 ) then
01165       gamma = za * gam ( z )
01166       exit
01167     else if ( z == 1.0D+00 ) then
01168       gamma = za
01169       exit
01170     end if
01171 
01172     za = za * z
01173 
01174   end do
01175 
01176   return
01177 end
01178 subroutine hermite_com ( norder, xtab, weight )
01179 !
01180 !*******************************************************************************
01181 !
01182 !! HERMITE_COM computes the abscissa and weights for Gauss-Hermite quadrature.
01183 !
01184 !
01185 !  Discussion:
01186 !
01187 !    The abscissas are the zeros of the N-th order Hermite polynomial.
01188 !
01189 !  Integration interval:
01190 !
01191 !    ( -Infinity, +Infinity )
01192 !
01193 !  Weight function:
01194 !
01195 !    EXP ( - X**2 )
01196 !
01197 !  Integral to approximate:
01198 !
01199 !    Integral ( -INFINITY < X < +INFINITY ) EXP ( - X**2 ) * F(X) dX
01200 !
01201 !  Approximate integral:
01202 !
01203 !    Sum ( 1 <= I <= NORDER ) WEIGHT(I) * F ( XTAB(I) )
01204 !
01205 !  Reference:
01206 !
01207 !    Arthur Stroud and Don Secrest,
01208 !    Gaussian Quadrature Formulas,
01209 !    Prentice Hall, 1966.
01210 !
01211 !  Modified:
01212 !
01213 !    19 September 1998
01214 !
01215 !  Author:
01216 !
01217 !    John Burkardt
01218 !
01219 !  Parameters:
01220 !
01221 !    Input, integer NORDER, the order of the formula to be computed.
01222 !
01223 !    Output, double precision XTAB(NORDER), the Gauss-Hermite abscissas.
01224 !
01225 !    Output, double precision WEIGHT(NORDER), the Gauss-Hermite weights.
01226 !
01227   implicit none
01228 !
01229   integer norder
01230 !
01231   double precision cc
01232   double precision dp2
01233   double precision gamma
01234   integer i
01235   double precision p1
01236   double precision s
01237   double precision temp
01238   double precision weight(norder)
01239   double precision x
01240   double precision xtab(norder)
01241 !
01242   cc = 1.7724538509D+00 * gamma ( dble ( norder ) ) / ( 2.0D+00**( norder - 1 ) )
01243 
01244   s = ( 2.0D+00 * dble ( norder ) + 1.0D+00 )**( 1.0D+00 / 6.0D+00 )
01245 
01246   do i = 1, ( norder + 1 ) / 2
01247 
01248     if ( i == 1 ) then
01249 
01250       x = s**3 - 1.85575D+00 / s
01251 
01252     else if ( i == 2 ) then
01253 
01254       x = x - 1.14D+00 * ( ( dble ( norder ) )**0.426D+00 ) / x
01255 
01256     else if ( i == 3 ) then
01257 
01258       x = 1.86D+00 * x - 0.86D+00 * xtab(1)
01259 
01260     else if ( i == 4 ) then
01261 
01262       x = 1.91D+00 * x - 0.91D+00 * xtab(2)
01263 
01264     else
01265 
01266       x = 2.0D+00 * x - xtab(i-2)
01267 
01268     end if
01269 
01270     call hermite_root ( x, norder, dp2, p1 )
01271 
01272     xtab(i) = x
01273     weight(i) = ( cc / dp2 ) / p1
01274 
01275     xtab(norder-i+1) = - x
01276     weight(norder-i+1) = weight(i)
01277 
01278   end do
01279 !
01280 !  Reverse the order of the XTAB values.
01281 !
01282   call dvec_reverse ( norder, xtab )
01283 
01284   return
01285 end
01286 subroutine hermite_recur ( p2, dp2, p1, x, norder )
01287 !
01288 !*******************************************************************************
01289 !
01290 !! HERMITE_RECUR finds the value and derivative of a Hermite polynomial.
01291 !
01292 !
01293 !  Reference:
01294 !
01295 !    Arthur Stroud and Don Secrest,
01296 !    Gaussian Quadrature Formulas,
01297 !    Prentice Hall, 1966.
01298 !
01299 !  Modified:
01300 !
01301 !    19 September 1998
01302 !
01303 !  Parameters:
01304 !
01305 !    Output, double precision P2, the value of H(NORDER)(X).
01306 !
01307 !    Output, double precision DP2, the value of H'(NORDER)(X).
01308 !
01309 !    Output, double precision P1, the value of H(NORDER-1)(X).
01310 !
01311 !    Input, double precision X, the point at which polynomials are evaluated.
01312 !
01313 !    Input, integer NORDER, the order of the polynomial to be computed.
01314 !
01315   implicit none
01316 !
01317   integer i
01318   double precision dp0
01319   double precision dp1
01320   double precision dp2
01321   integer norder
01322   double precision p0
01323   double precision p1
01324   double precision p2
01325   double precision x
01326 !
01327   p1 = 1.0D+00
01328   dp1 = 0.0D+00
01329 
01330   p2 = x
01331   dp2 = 1.0D+00
01332 
01333   do i = 2, norder
01334 
01335     p0 = p1
01336     dp0 = dp1
01337 
01338     p1 = p2
01339     dp1 = dp2
01340 
01341     p2  = x * p1 - 0.5D+00 * ( dble ( i ) - 1.0D+00 ) * p0
01342     dp2 = x * dp1 + p1 - 0.5D+00 * ( dble ( i ) - 1.0D+00 ) * dp0
01343 
01344   end do
01345 
01346   return
01347 end
01348 subroutine hermite_root ( x, norder, dp2, p1 )
01349 !
01350 !*******************************************************************************
01351 !
01352 !! HERMITE_ROOT improves an approximate root of a Hermite polynomial.
01353 !
01354 !
01355 !  Reference:
01356 !
01357 !    Arthur Stroud and Don Secrest,
01358 !    Gaussian Quadrature Formulas,
01359 !    Prentice Hall, 1966.
01360 !
01361 !  Modified:
01362 !
01363 !    19 September 1998
01364 !
01365 !  Parameters:
01366 !
01367 !    Input/output, double precision X, the approximate root, which
01368 !    should be improved on output.
01369 !
01370 !    Input, integer NORDER, the order of the Hermite polynomial.
01371 !
01372 !    Output, double precision DP2, the value of H'(NORDER)(X).
01373 !
01374 !    Output, double precision P1, the value of H(NORDER-1)(X).
01375 !
01376   implicit none
01377 !
01378   double precision d
01379   double precision dp2
01380   double precision, parameter :: eps = 1.0D-12
01381   integer i
01382   integer, parameter :: maxstep = 10
01383   integer norder
01384   double precision p1
01385   double precision p2
01386   double precision x
01387 !
01388   do i = 1, maxstep
01389 
01390     call hermite_recur ( p2, dp2, p1, x, norder )
01391 
01392     d = p2 / dp2
01393     x = x - d
01394 
01395     if ( abs ( d ) <= eps * ( abs ( x ) + 1.0D+00 ) ) then
01396       return
01397     end if
01398 
01399   end do
01400 
01401   return
01402 end
01403 subroutine hermite_set ( norder, xtab, weight )
01404 !
01405 !*******************************************************************************
01406 !
01407 !! HERMITE_SET sets abscissas and weights for Hermite quadrature.
01408 !
01409 !
01410 !  Integration interval:
01411 !
01412 !    ( -Infinity, +Infinity )
01413 !
01414 !  Weight function:
01415 !
01416 !    EXP ( - X**2 )
01417 !
01418 !  Integral to approximate:
01419 !
01420 !    Integral ( -INFINITY < X < +INFINITY ) EXP ( - X**2 ) * F(X) dX
01421 !
01422 !  Approximate integral:
01423 !
01424 !    Sum ( 1 <= I <= NORDER ) WEIGHT(I) * F ( XTAB(I) ).
01425 !
01426 !  Reference:
01427 !
01428 !    Abramowitz and Stegun,
01429 !    Handbook of Mathematical Functions,
01430 !    National Bureau of Standards, 1964.
01431 !
01432 !    Vladimir Krylov,
01433 !    Approximate Calculation of Integrals,
01434 !    MacMillan, 1962.
01435 !
01436 !    Arthur Stroud and Don Secrest,
01437 !    Gaussian Quadrature Formulas,
01438 !    Prentice Hall, 1966.
01439 !
01440 !    Daniel Zwillinger, editor,
01441 !    Standard Mathematical Tables and Formulae,
01442 !    30th Edition,
01443 !    CRC Press, 1996.
01444 !
01445 !  Modified:
01446 !
01447 !    06 December 2000
01448 !
01449 !  Author:
01450 !
01451 !    John Burkardt
01452 !
01453 !  Parameters:
01454 !
01455 !    Input, integer NORDER, the order of the rule.
01456 !    NORDER must be between 1 and 20, or one of the values
01457 !    30, 32, 40, 50, 60 or 64.
01458 !
01459 !    Output, double precision XTAB(NORDER), the abscissas of the rule,
01460 !    which are symmetrically placed around 0.
01461 !
01462 !    Output, double precision WEIGHT(NORDER), the weights of the rule.
01463 !    The weights are positive and symmetric, and should sum
01464 !    to SQRT(PI).
01465 !
01466   implicit none
01467 !
01468   integer norder

01472   double precision weight(norder)

01474   if ( norder == 1 ) then

02560

02563 subroutine jacobi_com ( norder, xtab, weight, alpha, beta )
02564 !
02565 !*******************************************************************************
02566 !
02567 !! JACOBI_COM computes the abscissa and weights for Gauss-Jacobi quadrature.
02568 !
02569 !
02570 !  Integration interval:
02571 !
02572 !    [ -1, 1 ]
02573 !
02574 !  Weight function:
02575 !
02576 !    1.0D+00
02577 !
02578 !  Integral to approximate:
02579 !
02580 !    Integral ( -1 <= X <= 1 ) (1+X)**ALPHA * (1-X)**BETA * F(X) dX
02581 !
02582 !  Approximate integral:
02583 !
02584 !    Sum ( 1 <= I <= NORDER ) WEIGHT(I) * F ( XTAB(I) )
02585 !
02586 !  Reference:
02587 !
02588 !    Arthur Stroud and Don Secrest,
02589 !    Gaussian Quadrature Formulas,
02590 !    Prentice Hall, 1966.
02591 !
02592 !  Modified:
02593 !
02594 !    09 September 2000
02595 !
02596 !  Parameters:
02597 !
02598 !    Input, integer NORDER, the order of the quadrature rule to be computed.
02599 !
02600 !    Output, double precision XTAB(NORDER), the Gauss-Jacobi abscissas.
02601 !
02602 !    Output, double precision WEIGHT(NORDER), the Gauss-Jacobi weights.
02603 !
02604 !    Input, double precision ALPHA, BETA, the exponents of (1+X) and
02605 !    (1-X) in the quadrature rule.  For simple Gauss-Legendre quadrature,
02606 !    set ALPHA = BETA = 0.0.
02607 !
02608   implicit none
02609 !
02610   integer norder
02611 !
02612   double precision alpha
02613   double precision an
02614   double precision b(norder)
02615   double precision beta
02616   double precision bn
02617   double precision c(norder)
02618   double precision cc
02619   double precision delta
02620   double precision dp2
02621   double precision log_gamma
02622   integer i
02623   double precision p1
02624   double precision r1
02625   double precision r2
02626   double precision r3
02627   double precision temp
02628   double precision weight(norder)
02629   double precision x
02630   double precision xtab(norder)
02631 !
02632 !  Set the recursion coefficients.
02633 !
02634   do i = 1, norder
02635 
02636     if ( alpha + beta == 0.0D+00 .or. beta - alpha == 0.0D+00) then
02637 
02638       b(i) = 0.0D+00
02639 
02640     else
02641 
02642       b(i) = ( alpha + beta ) * ( beta - alpha ) / &
02643             ( ( alpha + beta + dble ( 2 * i ) ) &
02644             * ( alpha + beta + dble ( 2 * i - 2 ) ) )
02645 
02646     end if
02647 
02648     if ( i == 1 ) then
02649 
02650       c(i) = 0.0D+00
02651 
02652     else
02653 
02654       c(i) = 4.0D+00 * dble ( i - 1 ) * ( alpha + dble ( i - 1 ) ) &
02655             * ( beta + dble ( i - 1 ) ) &
02656             * ( alpha + beta + dble ( i - 1 ) ) / &
02657             ( ( alpha + beta + dble ( 2 * i - 1 ) ) &
02658             * ( alpha + beta + dble ( 2 * i - 2 ) )**2 &
02659             * ( alpha + beta + dble ( 2 * i - 3 ) ) )
02660 
02661     end if
02662 
02663   end do
02664 
02665   delta = exp ( log_gamma ( alpha + 1.0D+00 ) + log_gamma ( beta + 1.0D+00) &
02666     + log_gamma ( alpha + beta + 2.0D+00 ) )
02667 
02668   cc = delta * 2.0D+00**( alpha + beta + 1.0D+00 ) * product ( c(2:norder) )
02669 
02670   do i = 1, norder
02671 
02672     if ( i == 1 ) then
02673 
02674       an = alpha / dble ( norder )
02675       bn = beta / dble ( norder )
02676 
02677       r1 = ( 1.0D+00 + alpha ) * ( 2.78D+00 / ( 4.0D+00+ dble ( norder**2 ) ) &
02678         + 0.768D+00 * an / dble ( norder ) )
02679 
02680       r2 = 1.0D+00 + 1.48D+00 * an + 0.96D+00 * bn &
02681         + 0.452D+00 * an**2 + 0.83D+00 * an * bn
02682 
02683       x = ( r2 - r1 ) / r2
02684 
02685     else if ( i == 2 ) then
02686 
02687       r1 = ( 4.1D+00 + alpha ) / &
02688         ( ( 1.0D+00 + alpha ) * ( 1.0D+00 + 0.156D+00 * alpha ) )
02689 
02690       r2 = 1.0D+00 + 0.06D+00 * ( dble ( norder ) - 8.0D+00 ) * &
02691         ( 1.0D+00 + 0.12D+00 * alpha ) / dble ( norder )
02692 
02693       r3 = 1.0D+00 + 0.012D+00 * beta * &
02694         ( 1.0D+00 + 0.25D+00 * abs ( alpha ) ) / dble ( norder )
02695 
02696       x = x - r1 * r2 * r3 * ( 1.0D+00 - x )
02697 
02698     else if ( i == 3 ) then
02699 
02700       r1 = ( 1.67D+00 + 0.28D+00 * alpha ) / ( 1.0D+00 + 0.37D+00 * alpha )
02701 
02702       r2 = 1.0D+00 + 0.22D+00 * ( dble ( norder ) - 8.0D+00 ) / dble ( norder )
02703 
02704       r3 = 1.0D+00 + 8.0D+00 * beta / &
02705         ( ( 6.28D+00 + beta ) * dble ( norder**2 ) )
02706 
02707       x = x - r1 * r2 * r3 * ( xtab(1) - x )
02708 
02709     else if ( i < norder - 1 ) then
02710 
02711       x = 3.0D+00 * xtab(i-1) - 3.0D+00 * xtab(i-2) + xtab(i-3)
02712 
02713     else if ( i == norder - 1 ) then
02714 
02715       r1 = ( 1.0D+00 + 0.235D+00 * beta ) / ( 0.766D+00 + 0.119D+00 * beta )
02716 
02717       r2 = 1.0D+00 / ( 1.0D+00 + 0.639D+00 * ( dble ( norder ) - 4.0D+00 ) &
02718         / ( 1.0D+00 + 0.71D+00 * ( dble ( norder ) - 4.0D+00 ) ) )
02719 
02720       r3 = 1.0D+00 / ( 1.0D+00 + 20.0D+00 * alpha / ( ( 7.5D+00 + alpha ) * &
02721         dble ( norder**2 ) ) )
02722 
02723       x = x + r1 * r2 * r3 * ( x - xtab(i-2) )
02724 
02725     else if ( i == norder ) then
02726 
02727       r1 = ( 1.0D+00 + 0.37D+00 * beta ) / ( 1.67D+00 + 0.28D+00 * beta )
02728 
02729       r2 = 1.0D+00 / &
02730         ( 1.0D+00 + 0.22D+00 * ( dble ( norder ) - 8.0D+00 ) / dble ( norder ) )
02731 
02732       r3 = 1.0D+00 / ( 1.0D+00 + 8.0D+00 * alpha / &
02733         ( ( 6.28D+00 + alpha ) * dble ( norder**2 ) ) )
02734 
02735       x = x + r1 * r2 * r3 * ( x - xtab(i-2) )
02736 
02737     end if
02738 
02739     call jacobi_root ( x, norder, alpha, beta, dp2, p1, b, c )
02740 
02741     xtab(i) = x
02742     weight(i) = cc / ( dp2 * p1 )
02743 
02744   end do
02745 !
02746 !  Reverse the order of the XTAB values.
02747 !
02748   call dvec_reverse ( norder, xtab )
02749 
02750   return
02751 end
02752 subroutine jacobi_recur ( p2, dp2, p1, x, norder, alpha, beta, b, c )
02753 !
02754 !*******************************************************************************
02755 !
02756 !! JACOBI_RECUR finds the value and derivative of a Jacobi polynomial.
02757 !
02758 !
02759 !  Reference:
02760 !
02761 !    Arthur Stroud and Don Secrest,
02762 !    Gaussian Quadrature Formulas,
02763 !    Prentice Hall, 1966.
02764 !
02765 !  Modified:
02766 !
02767 !    19 September 1998
02768 !
02769 !  Parameters:
02770 !
02771 !    Output, double precision P2, the value of J(NORDER)(X).
02772 !
02773 !    Output, double precision DP2, the value of J'(NORDER)(X).
02774 !
02775 !    Output, double precision P1, the value of J(NORDER-1)(X).
02776 !
02777 !    Input, double precision X, the point at which polynomials are evaluated.
02778 !
02779 !    Input, integer NORDER, the order of the polynomial to be computed.
02780 !
02781 !    Input, double precision ALPHA, BETA, the exponents of (1+X) and
02782 !    (1-X) in the quadrature rule.
02783 !
02784 !    Input, double precision B(NORDER), C(NORDER), the recursion
02785 !    coefficients.
02786 !
02787   implicit none
02788 !
02789   integer norder
02790 !
02791   double precision alpha
02792   double precision b(norder)
02793   double precision beta
02794   double precision c(norder)
02795   double precision dp0
02796   double precision dp1
02797   double precision dp2
02798   integer i
02799   double precision p0
02800   double precision p1
02801   double precision p2
02802   double precision x
02803 !
02804   p1 = 1.0D+00
02805   dp1 = 0.0D+00
02806 
02807   p2 = x + ( alpha - beta ) / ( alpha + beta + 2.0D+00 )
02808   dp2 = 1.0D+00
02809 
02810   do i = 2, norder
02811 
02812     p0 = p1
02813     dp0 = dp1
02814 
02815     p1 = p2
02816     dp1 = dp2
02817 
02818     p2 = ( x - b(i) ) * p1 - c(i) * p0
02819     dp2 = ( x - b(i) ) * dp1 + p1 - c(i) * dp0
02820 
02821   end do
02822 
02823   return
02824 end
02825 subroutine jacobi_root ( x, norder, alpha, beta, dp2, p1, b, c )
02826 !
02827 !*******************************************************************************
02828 !
02829 !! JACOBI_ROOT improves an approximate root of a Jacobi polynomial.
02830 !
02831 !
02832 !  Reference:
02833 !
02834 !    Arthur Stroud and Don Secrest,
02835 !    Gaussian Quadrature Formulas,
02836 !    Prentice Hall, 1966.
02837 !
02838 !  Modified:
02839 !
02840 !    09 December 2000
02841 !
02842 !  Parameters:
02843 !
02844 !    Input/output, double precision X, the approximate root, which
02845 !    should be improved on output.
02846 !
02847 !    Input, integer NORDER, the order of the polynomial to be computed.
02848 !
02849 !    Input, double precision ALPHA, BETA, the exponents of (1+X) and
02850 !    (1-X) in the quadrature rule.
02851 !
02852 !    Output, double precision DP2, the value of J'(NORDER)(X).
02853 !
02854 !    Output, double precision P1, the value of J(NORDER-1)(X).
02855 !
02856 !    Input, double precision B(NORDER), C(NORDER), the recursion coefficients.
02857 !
02858   implicit none
02859 !
02860   integer norder
02861 !
02862   double precision alpha
02863   double precision b(norder)
02864   double precision beta
02865   double precision c(norder)
02866   double precision d
02867   double precision dp2
02868   double precision eps
02869   integer i
02870   integer, parameter :: maxstep = 10
02871   double precision p1
02872   double precision p2
02873   double precision x
02874 !
02875   eps = epsilon ( x )
02876 
02877   do i = 1, maxstep
02878 
02879     call jacobi_recur ( p2, dp2, p1, x, norder, alpha, beta, b, c )
02880 
02881     d = p2 / dp2
02882     x = x - d
02883 
02884     if ( abs ( d ) <= eps * ( abs ( x ) + 1.0D+00 ) ) then
02885       return
02886     end if
02887 
02888   end do
02889 
02890   return
02891 end
02892 subroutine kronrod_set ( norder, xtab, weight )
02893 !
02894 !*******************************************************************************
02895 !
02896 !! KRONROD_SET sets abscissas and weights for Gauss-Kronrod quadrature.
02897 !
02898 !
02899 !  Integration interval:
02900 !
02901 !    [ -1, 1 ]
02902 !
02903 !  Weight function:
02904 !
02905 !    1.0D+00
02906 !
02907 !  Integral to approximate:
02908 !
02909 !    Integral ( -1 <= X <= 1 ) F(X) dX
02910 !
02911 !  Approximate integral:
02912 !
02913 !    Sum ( 1 <= I <= NORDER ) WEIGHT(I) * F ( XTAB(I) )
02914 !
02915 !  Note:
02916 !
02917 !    A Kronrod rule is used in conjunction with a lower order
02918 !    Gauss rule, and provides an efficient error estimation.
02919 !
02920 !    The error may be estimated as the difference in the two integral
02921 !    approximations.
02922 !
02923 !    The efficiency comes about because the Kronrod uses the abscissas
02924 !    of the Gauss rule, thus saving on the number of function evaluations
02925 !    necessary.  If the Kronrod rule were replaced by a Gauss rule of
02926 !    the same order, a higher precision integral estimate would be
02927 !    made, but the function would have to be evaluated at many more
02928 !    points.
02929 !
02930 !    The Gauss Kronrod pair of rules involves an ( NORDER + 1 ) / 2
02931 !    point Gauss-Legendre rule and an NORDER point Kronrod rule.
02932 !    Thus, the 15 point Kronrod rule should be paired with the
02933 !    Gauss-Legendre 7 point rule.
02934 !
02935 !  Reference:
02936 !
02937 !    R Piessens, E de Doncker-Kapenger, C Ueberhuber, D Kahaner,
02938 !    QUADPACK, A Subroutine Package for Automatic Integration,
02939 !    Springer Verlag, 1983.
02940 !
02941 !  Modified:
02942 !
02943 !    16 September 1998
02944 !
02945 !  Author:
02946 !
02947 !    John Burkardt
02948 !
02949 !  Parameters:
02950 !
02951 !    Input, integer NORDER, the order of the rule, which may be
02952 !    15, 21, 31 or 41, corresponding to Gauss-Legendre rules of
02953 !    order 7, 10, 15 or 20.
02954 !
02955 !    Output, double precision XTAB(NORDER), the abscissas of the rule, which
02956 !    are symmetrically places in [-1,1].
02957 !
02958 !    Output, double precision WEIGHT(NORDER), the weights of the rule.
02959 !    The weights are positive, symmetric, and should sum to 2.
02960 !
02961   implicit none
02962 !
02963   integer norder
02964 !
02965   double precision weight(norder)
02966   double precision xtab(norder)
02967 !
02968   if ( norder == 15 ) then
02969 
02970     xtab(1) =  - 0.9914553711208126D+00
02971     xtab(2) =  - 0.9491079123427585D+00
02972     xtab(3) =  - 0.8648644233597691D+00
02973     xtab(4) =  - 0.7415311855993944D+00
02974     xtab(5) =  - 0.5860872354676911D+00
02975     xtab(6) =  - 0.4058451513773972D+00
02976     xtab(7) =  - 0.2077849550789850D+00
02977     xtab(8) =    0.0D+00
02978     xtab(9) =    0.2077849550789850D+00
02979     xtab(10) =   0.4058451513773972D+00
02980     xtab(11) =   0.5860872354676911D+00
02981     xtab(12) =   0.7415311855993944D+00
02982     xtab(13) =   0.8648644233597691D+00
02983     xtab(14) =   0.9491079123427585D+00
02984     xtab(15) =   0.9914553711208126D+00
02985 
02986     weight(1) =  0.2293532201052922D-01
02987     weight(2) =  0.6309209262997855D-01
02988     weight(3) =  0.1047900103222502D+00
02989     weight(4) =  0.1406532597155259D+00
02990     weight(5) =  0.1690047266392679D+00
02991     weight(6) =  0.1903505780647854D+00
02992     weight(7) =  0.2044329400752989D+00
02993     weight(8) =  0.2094821410847278D+00
02994     weight(9) =  0.2044329400752989D+00
02995     weight(10) = 0.1903505780647854D+00
02996     weight(11) = 0.1690047266392679D+00
02997     weight(12) = 0.1406532597155259D+00
02998     weight(13) = 0.1047900103222502D+00
02999     weight(14) = 0.6309209262997855D-01
03000     weight(15) = 0.2293532201052922D-01
03001 
03002   else if ( norder == 21 ) then
03003 
03004     xtab(1) =  - 0.9956571630258081D+00
03005     xtab(2) =  - 0.9739065285171717D+00
03006     xtab(3) =  - 0.9301574913557082D+00
03007     xtab(4) =  - 0.8650633666889845D+00

03009     xtab(6) =  - 0.6794095682990244D+00

03212 subroutine laguerre_com ( norder, xtab, weight, alpha )
03213 !
03214 !*******************************************************************************
03215 !
03216 !! LAGUERRE_COM computes the abscissa and weights for Gauss-Laguerre quadrature.
03217 !
03218 !
03219 !  Discussion:
03220 !
03221 !    In the simplest case, ALPHA is 0, and we are approximating the
03222 !    integral from 0 to INFINITY of EXP(-X) * F(X).  When this is so,
03223 !    it is easy to modify the rule to approximate the integral from
03224 !    A to INFINITY as well.
03225 !
03226 !    If ALPHA is nonzero, then there is no simple way to extend the
03227 !    rule to approximate the integral from A to INFINITY.  The simplest
03228 !    procedures would be to approximate the integral from 0 to A.
03229 !
03230 !  Integration interval:
03231 !
03232 !      [ A, +Infinity ) or [ 0, +Infinity )
03233 !
03234 !  Weight function:
03235 !
03236 !      EXP ( - X ) or EXP ( - X ) * X**ALPHA
03237 !
03238 !  Integral to approximate:
03239 !
03240 !      Integral ( A <= X < +INFINITY ) EXP ( - X ) * F(X) dX
03241 !    or
03242 !      Integral ( 0 <= X < +INFINITY ) EXP ( - X ) * X**ALPHA * F(X) dX
03243 !
03244 !  Approximate integral:
03245 !
03246 !      EXP ( - A ) * Sum ( 1 <= I <= NORDER ) WEIGHT(I) * F ( A+XTAB(I) )
03247 !    or
03248 !      Sum ( 1 <= I <= NORDER ) WEIGHT(I) * F ( XTAB(I) )
03249 !
03250 !  Reference:
03251 !
03252 !    Arthur Stroud and Don Secrest,
03253 !    Gaussian Quadrature Formulas,
03254 !    Prentice Hall, 1966.
03255 !
03256 !  Modified:
03257 !
03258 !    15 March 2000
03259 !
03260 !  Parameters:
03261 !
03262 !    Input, integer NORDER, the order of the quadrature rule to be computed.
03263 !    NORDER must be at least 1.
03264 !
03265 !    Output, double precision XTAB(NORDER), the Gauss-Laguerre abscissas.
03266 !
03267 !    Output, double precision WEIGHT(NORDER), the Gauss-Laguerre weights.
03268 !
03269 !    Input, double precision ALPHA, the exponent of the X factor.
03270 !    Set ALPHA = 0.0D+00 for the simplest rule.
03271 !    ALPHA must be nonnegative.
03272 !
03273   implicit none
03274 !
03275   integer norder
03276 !
03277   double precision alpha
03278   double precision b(norder)
03279   double precision c(norder)
03280   double precision cc
03281   double precision dp2
03282   double precision gamma
03283   integer i
03284   double precision p1
03285   double precision r1
03286   double precision r2
03287   double precision ratio
03288   double precision weight(norder)
03289   double precision x
03290   double precision xtab(norder)
03291 !
03292 !  Set the recursion coefficients.
03293 !
03294   do i = 1, norder
03295     b(i) = ( alpha + dble ( 2 * i - 1 ) )
03296   end do
03297 
03298   do i = 1, norder
03299     c(i) = dble ( i - 1 ) * ( alpha + dble ( i - 1 ) )
03300   end do
03301 
03302   cc = gamma ( alpha + 1.0D+00 ) * product ( c(2:norder) )
03303 
03304   do i = 1, norder
03305 !
03306 !  Compute an estimate for the root.
03307 !
03308     if ( i == 1 ) then
03309 
03310       x = ( 1.0D+00 + alpha ) * ( 3.0D+00+ 0.92 * alpha ) / &
03311         ( 1.0D+00 + 2.4D+00 * dble ( norder ) + 1.8D+00 * alpha )
03312 
03313     else if ( i == 2 ) then
03314 
03315       x = x + ( 15.0D+00 + 6.25D+00 * alpha ) / &
03316         ( 1.0D+00 + 0.9D+00 * alpha + 2.5D+00 * dble ( norder ) )
03317 
03318     else
03319 
03320       r1 = ( 1.0D+00 + 2.55D+00 * dble ( i - 2 ) ) / ( 1.9D+00 * dble ( i - 2 ) )
03321 
03322       r2 = 1.26D+00 * dble ( i - 2 ) * alpha / &
03323         ( 1.0D+00 + 3.5D+00 * dble ( i - 2 ) )
03324 
03325       ratio = ( r1 + r2 ) / ( 1.0D+00 + 0.3D+00 * alpha )
03326 
03327       x = x + ratio * ( x - xtab(i-2) )
03328 
03329     end if
03330 !
03331 !  Use iteration to find the root.
03332 !
03333     call laguerre_root ( x, norder, alpha, dp2, p1, b, c )
03334 !
03335 !  Set the abscissa and weight.
03336 !
03337     xtab(i) = x
03338     weight(i) = ( cc / dp2 ) / p1
03339 
03340   end do
03341 
03342   return
03343 end
03344 subroutine laguerre_recur ( p2, dp2, p1, x, norder, alpha, b, c )
03345 !
03346 !*******************************************************************************
03347 !
03348 !! LAGUERRE_RECUR finds the value and derivative of a Laguerre polynomial.
03349 !
03350 !
03351 !  Reference:
03352 !
03353 !    Arthur Stroud and Don Secrest,
03354 !    Gaussian Quadrature Formulas,
03355 !    Prentice Hall, 1966.
03356 !
03357 !  Modified:
03358 !
03359 !    19 September 1998
03360 !
03361 !  Parameters:
03362 !
03363 !    Output, double precision P2, the value of L(NORDER)(X).
03364 !
03365 !    Output, double precision DP2, the value of L'(NORDER)(X).
03366 !
03367 !    Output, double precision P1, the value of L(NORDER-1)(X).
03368 !
03369 !    Input, double precision X, the point at which polynomials are evaluated.
03370 !
03371 !    Input, integer NORDER, the order of the polynomial to be computed.
03372 !
03373 !    Input, double precision ALPHA, the exponent of the X factor in the
03374 !    integrand.
03375 !
03376 !    Input, double precision B(NORDER), C(NORDER), the recursion
03377 !    coefficients.
03378 !
03379   implicit none
03380 !
03381   integer norder
03382 !
03383   double precision alpha
03384   double precision b(norder)
03385   double precision c(norder)
03386   double precision dp0
03387   double precision dp1
03388   double precision dp2
03389   integer i
03390   double precision p0
03391   double precision p1
03392   double precision p2
03393   double precision x
03394 !
03395   p1 = 1.0D+00
03396   dp1 = 0.0D+00
03397 
03398   p2 = x - alpha - 1.0D+00
03399   dp2 = 1.0D+00
03400 
03401   do i = 2, norder
03402 
03403     p0 = p1
03404     dp0 = dp1
03405 
03406     p1 = p2
03407     dp1 = dp2
03408 
03409     p2 = ( x - b(i) ) * p1 - c(i) * p0
03410     dp2 = ( x - b(i) ) * dp1 + p1 - c(i) * dp0
03411 
03412   end do
03413 
03414   return
03415 end
03416 subroutine laguerre_root ( x, norder, alpha, dp2, p1, b, c )
03417 !
03418 !*******************************************************************************
03419 !
03420 !! LAGUERRE_ROOT improves an approximate root of a Laguerre polynomial.
03421 !
03422 !
03423 !  Reference:
03424 !
03425 !    Arthur Stroud and Don Secrest,
03426 !    Gaussian Quadrature Formulas,
03427 !    Prentice Hall, 1966.
03428 !
03429 !  Modified:
03430 !
03431 !    09 December 2000
03432 !
03433 !  Parameters:
03434 !
03435 !    Input/output, double precision X, the approximate root, which
03436 !    should be improved on output.
03437 !
03438 !    Input, integer NORDER, the order of the polynomial to be computed.
03439 !
03440 !    Input, double precision ALPHA, the exponent of the X factor.
03441 !
03442 !    Output, double precision DP2, the value of L'(NORDER)(X).
03443 !
03444 !    Output, double precision P1, the value of L(NORDER-1)(X).
03445 !
03446 !    Input, double precision B(NORDER), C(NORDER), the recursion coefficients.
03447 !
03448   implicit none
03449 !
03450   integer norder
03451 !
03452   double precision alpha
03453   double precision b(norder)
03454   double precision c(norder)
03455   double precision d
03456   double precision dp2
03457   double precision eps
03458   integer i
03459   integer, parameter :: maxstep = 10
03460   double precision p1
03461   double precision p2
03462   double precision x
03463 !
03464   eps = epsilon ( x )
03465 
03466   do i = 1, maxstep
03467 
03468     call laguerre_recur ( p2, dp2, p1, x, norder, alpha, b, c )
03469 
03470     d = p2 / dp2
03471     x = x - d
03472 
03473     if ( abs ( d ) <= eps * ( abs ( x ) + 1.0D+00 ) ) then
03474       return
03475     end if
03476 
03477   end do
03478 
03479   return
03480 end
03481 subroutine laguerre_set ( norder, xtab, weight )
03482 !
03483 !*******************************************************************************
03484 !
03485 !! LAGUERRE_SET sets abscissas and weights for Laguerre quadrature.
03486 !
03487 !
03488 !  Integration interval:
03489 !
03490 !    [ 0, +Infinity )
03491 !
03492 !  Weight function:
03493 !
03494 !    EXP ( - X )
03495 !
03496 !  Integral to approximate:
03497 !
03498 !    Integral ( 0 <= X < +INFINITY ) EXP ( - X ) * F(X) dX
03499 !
03500 !  Approximate integral:
03501 !
03502 !    Sum ( 1 <= I <= NORDER ) WEIGHT(I) * F ( XTAB(I) )
03503 !
03504 !  Note:
03505 !
03506 !    The abscissas are the zeroes of the Laguerre polynomial L(NORDER)(X).
03507 !
03508 !  Reference:
03509 !
03510 !    Abramowitz and Stegun,
03511 !    Handbook of Mathematical Functions,
03512 !    National Bureau of Standards, 1964.
03513 !
03514 !    Vladimir Krylov,
03515 !    Approximate Calculation of Integrals,
03516 !    MacMillan, 1962.
03517 !
03518 !    Arthur Stroud and Don Secrest,
03519 !    Gaussian Quadrature Formulas,
03520 !    Prentice Hall, 1966.
03521 !
03522 !    Daniel Zwillinger, editor,
03523 !    Standard Mathematical Tables and Formulae,
03524 !    30th Edition,
03525 !    CRC Press, 1996.
03526 !
03527 !  Modified:
03528 !
03529 !    17 September 1998
03530 !
03531 !  Author:
03532 !
03533 !    John Burkardt
03534 !
03535 !  Parameters:
03536 !
03537 !    Input, integer NORDER, the order of the rule.
03538 !    NORDER must be between 1 and 20.
03539 !
03540 !    Output, double precision XTAB(NORDER), the abscissas of the rule.
03541 !
03542 !    Output, double precision WEIGHT(NORDER), the weights of the rule.
03543 !    The weights are positive, and should add to 1.
03544 !
03545   implicit none
03546 !
03547   integer norder
03548 !
03549   double precision weight(norder)
03550   double precision xtab(norder)
03551 !
03552   if ( norder == 1 ) then
03553 
03554     xtab(1) =    1.0D+00
03555     weight(1) =  1.0D+00
03556

04063 subroutine laguerre_sum ( func, a, norder, xtab, weight, result )
04064 !
04065 !*******************************************************************************
04066 !
04067 !! LAGUERRE_SUM carries out Laguerre quadrature over [ A, +Infinity ).
04068 !
04069 !
04070 !  Discussion:
04071 !
04072 !    The simplest Laguerre integral to approximate is the
04073 !    integral from 0 to INFINITY of EXP(-X) * F(X).  When this is so,
04074 !    it is easy to modify the rule to approximate the integral from
04075 !    A to INFINITY as well.
04076 !
04077 !    Another common Laguerre integral to approximate is the
04078 !    integral from 0 to Infinity of EXP(-X) * X**ALPHA * F(X).
04079 !    This routine may be used to sum up the terms of the Laguerre
04080 !    rule for such an integral as well.  However, if ALPHA is nonzero,
04081 !    then there is no simple way to extend the rule to approximate the
04082 !    integral from A to INFINITY.  The simplest procedures would be
04083 !    to approximate the integral from 0 to A.
04084 !
04085 !  Integration interval:
04086 !
04087 !    [ A, +Infinity ) or [ 0, +Infinity )
04088 !
04089 !  Weight function:
04090 !
04091 !    EXP ( - X ) or EXP ( - X ) * X**ALPHA
04092 !
04093 !  Integral to approximate:
04094 !
04095 !    Integral ( A <= X <= +Infinity ) EXP ( -X ) * F(X) dX or
04096 !    Integral ( 0 <= X <= +Infinity ) EXP ( -X ) * X**ALPHA * F(X) dX
04097 !
04098 !  Approximate integral:
04099 !
04100 !    EXP ( - A ) * Sum ( 1 <= I <= NORDER ) WEIGHT(I) * F ( XTAB(I) + A ) 
04101 !
04102 !    or
04103 !
04104 !    Sum ( 1 <= I <= NORDER ) WEIGHT(I) * F ( XTAB(I) )
04105 !
04106 !  Reference:
04107 !
04108 !    Abramowitz and Stegun,
04109 !    Handbook of Mathematical Functions,
04110 !    National Bureau of Standards, 1964.
04111 !
04112 !    Daniel Zwillinger, editor,
04113 !    Standard Mathematical Tables and Formulae,
04114 !    30th Edition,
04115 !    CRC Press, 1996.
04116 !
04117 !  Modified:
04118 !
04119 !    15 March 2000
04120 !
04121 !  Author:
04122 !
04123 !    John Burkardt
04124 !
04125 !  Parameters:
04126 !
04127 !    Input, external FUNC, the name of the FORTRAN function which
04128 !    evaluates the integrand.  The function must have the form
04129 !      double precision func ( x ).
04130 !
04131 !    Input, double precision A, the beginning of the integration interval.
04132 !
04133 !    Input, integer NORDER, the order of the rule.
04134 !
04135 !    Input, double precision XTAB(NORDER), the abscissas of the rule.
04136 !
04137 !    Input, double precision WEIGHT(NORDER), the weights of the rule.
04138 !
04139 !    Output, double precision RESULT, the approximate value of the integral.
04140 !
04141   implicit none
04142 !
04143   integer norder
04144 !
04145   double precision a
04146   double precision, external :: func
04147   integer i
04148   double precision result
04149   double precision xtab(norder)
04150   double precision weight(norder)
04151 !
04152   if ( norder < 1 ) then
04153     write ( *, '(a)' ) ' '
04154     write ( *, '(a)' ) 'LAGUERRE_SUM - Fatal error!'
04155     write ( *, '(a,i6)' ) '  Nonpositive NORDER = ', norder
04156     stop
04157   end if
04158 
04159   result = 0.0D+00
04160   do i = 1, norder
04161     result = result + weight(i) * func ( xtab(i) + a )
04162   end do
04163   result = exp ( - a ) * result
04164 
04165   return
04166 end
04167 subroutine legendre_com ( norder, xtab, weight )
04168 !
04169 !*******************************************************************************
04170 !
04171 !! LEGENDRE_COM computes abscissas and weights for Gauss-Legendre quadrature.
04172 !
04173 !
04174 !  Integration interval:
04175 !
04176 !    [ -1, 1 ]
04177 !
04178 !  Weight function:
04179 !
04180 !    1.0D+00
04181 !
04182 !  Integral to approximate:
04183 !
04184 !    Integral ( -1 <= X <= 1 ) F(X) dX
04185 !
04186 !  Approximate integral:
04187 !
04188 !    Sum ( 1 <= I <= NORDER ) WEIGHT(I) * F ( XTAB(I) )
04189 !
04190 !  Modified:
04191 !
04192 !    16 September 1998
04193 !
04194 !  Parameters:
04195 !
04196 !    Input, integer NORDER, the order of the rule.
04197 !    NORDER must be greater than 0.
04198 !
04199 !    Output, double precision XTAB(NORDER), the abscissas of the rule.
04200 !
04201 !    Output, double precision WEIGHT(NORDER), the weights of the rule.
04202 !    The weights are positive, symmetric, and should sum to 2.
04203 !
04204   implicit none
04205 !
04206   integer norder
04207 !
04208   double precision d1
04209   double precision d2pn
04210   double precision d3pn
04211   double precision d4pn
04212   double precision dp
04213   double precision d_pi
04214   double precision dpn
04215   double precision e1
04216   double precision fx
04217   double precision h
04218   integer i
04219   integer iback
04220   integer k
04221   integer m
04222   integer mp1mi
04223   integer ncopy
04224   integer nmove
04225   double precision p
04226   double precision pk
04227   double precision pkm1
04228   double precision pkp1
04229   double precision t
04230   double precision u
04231   double precision v
04232   double precision x0
04233   double precision xtab(norder)
04234   double precision xtemp
04235   double precision weight(norder)
04236 !
04237   if ( norder < 1 ) then
04238     write ( *, '(a)' ) ' '
04239     write ( *, '(a)' ) 'LEGENDRE_COM - Fatal error!'
04240     write ( *, '(a,i6)' ) '  Illegal value of NORDER = ', norder
04241     stop
04242   end if
04243 
04244   e1 = dble ( norder * ( norder + 1 ) )
04245 
04246   m = ( norder + 1 ) / 2
04247 
04248   do i = 1, ( norder + 1 ) / 2
04249 
04250     mp1mi = m + 1 - i
04251     t = dble ( 4 * i - 1 ) * d_pi ( ) / dble ( 4 * norder + 2 )
04252     x0 = cos(t) * ( 1.0D+00 - ( 1.0D+00 - 1.0D+00 / dble ( norder ) ) &
04253       / dble ( 8 * norder**2 ) )
04254 
04255     pkm1 = 1.0D+00
04256     pk = x0
04257 
04258     do k = 2, norder
04259       pkp1 = 2.0D+00 * x0 * pk - pkm1 - ( x0 * pk - pkm1 ) / dble ( k )
04260       pkm1 = pk
04261       pk = pkp1
04262     end do
04263 
04264     d1 = dble ( norder ) * ( pkm1 - x0 * pk )
04265 
04266     dpn = d1 / ( 1.0D+00 - x0**2 )
04267 
04268     d2pn = ( 2.0D+00 * x0 * dpn - e1 * pk ) / ( 1.0D+00 - x0**2 )
04269 
04270     d3pn = ( 4.0D+00 * x0 * d2pn + ( 2.0D+00 - e1 ) * dpn ) &
04271       / ( 1.0D+00 - x0**2 )
04272 
04273     d4pn = ( 6.0D+00 * x0 * d3pn + ( 6.0D+00 - e1 ) * d2pn ) / &
04274       ( 1.0D+00 - x0**2 )
04275 
04276     u = pk / dpn
04277     v = d2pn / dpn
04278 !
04279 !  Initial approximation H:
04280 !
04281     h = - u * ( 1.0D+00 + 0.5D+00 * u * ( v + u * ( v**2 - d3pn / &
04282       ( 3.0D+00 * dpn ) ) ) )
04283 !
04284 !  Refine H using one step of Newton's method:
04285 !
04286     p = pk + h * ( dpn + 0.5D+00 * h * ( d2pn + h / 3.0D+00 &
04287       * ( d3pn + 0.25D+00 * h * d4pn ) ) )
04288 
04289     dp = dpn + h * ( d2pn + 0.5D+00 * h * ( d3pn + h * d4pn / 3.0D+00 ) )
04290 
04291     h = h - p / dp
04292 
04293     xtemp = x0 + h
04294 
04295     xtab(mp1mi) = xtemp
04296 
04297     fx = d1 - h * e1 * ( pk + 0.5D+00 * h * ( dpn + h / 3.0D+00 &
04298       * ( d2pn + 0.25D+00 * h * ( d3pn + 0.2D+00 * h * d4pn ) ) ) )
04299 
04300     weight(mp1mi) = 2.0D+00 * ( 1.0D+00 - xtemp**2 ) / fx**2
04301 
04302   end do
04303 
04304   if ( mod ( norder, 2 ) == 1 ) then
04305     xtab(1) = 0.0D+00
04306   end if
04307 !
04308 !  Shift the data up.
04309 !
04310   nmove = ( norder + 1 ) / 2
04311   ncopy = norder - nmove
04312 
04313   do i = 1, nmove
04314     iback = norder + 1 - i
04315     xtab(iback) = xtab(iback-ncopy)
04316     weight(iback) = weight(iback-ncopy)
04317   end do
04318 !
04319 !  Reflect values for the negative abscissas.
04320 !
04321   do i = 1, norder - nmove
04322     xtab(i) = - xtab(norder+1-i)
04323     weight(i) = weight(norder+1-i)
04324   end do
04325 
04326   return
04327 end
04328 subroutine legendre_recur ( p2, dp2, p1, x, norder )
04329 !
04330 !*******************************************************************************
04331 !
04332 !! LEGENDRE_RECUR finds the value and derivative of a Legendre polynomial.
04333 !
04334 !
04335 !  Reference:
04336 !
04337 !    Arthur Stroud and Don Secrest,
04338 !    Gaussian Quadrature Formulas,
04339 !    Prentice Hall, 1966.
04340 !
04341 !  Modified:
04342 !
04343 !    19 September 1998
04344 !
04345 !  Parameters:
04346 !
04347 !    Output, double precision P2, the value of P(NORDER)(X).
04348 !
04349 !    Output, double precision DP2, the value of P'(NORDER)(X).
04350 !
04351 !    Output, double precision P1, the value of P(NORDER-1)(X).
04352 !
04353 !    Input, double precision X, the point at which polynomials are evaluated.
04354 !
04355 !    Input, integer NORDER, the order of the polynomial to be computed.
04356 !
04357   implicit none
04358 !
04359   integer norder
04360 !
04361   double precision dp0
04362   double precision dp1
04363   double precision dp2
04364   integer i
04365   double precision p0
04366   double precision p1
04367   double precision p2
04368   double precision x
04369 !
04370   p1 = 1.0D+00
04371   dp1 = 0.0D+00
04372 
04373   p2 = x
04374   dp2 = 1.0D+00
04375 
04376   do i = 2, norder
04377 
04378     p0 = p1
04379     dp0 = dp1
04380 
04381     p1 = p2
04382     dp1 = dp2
04383 
04384     p2 = ( dble ( 2 * i - 1 ) * x * p1 - dble ( i - 1 ) * p0 ) / dble ( i )
04385 
04386     dp2 = ( dble ( 2 * i - 1 ) * ( p1 + x * dp1 ) - dble ( i - 1 ) * dp0 ) &
04387       / dble ( i )
04388 
04389   end do
04390 
04391   return
04392 end
04393 subroutine legendre_set ( norder, xtab, weight )
04394 !
04395 !*******************************************************************************
04396 !
04397 !! LEGENDRE_SET sets abscissas and weights for Gauss-Legendre quadrature.
04398 !
04399 !
04400 !  Integration interval:
04401 !
04402 !    [ -1, 1 ]
04403 !
04404 !  Weight function:
04405 !
04406 !    1.0D+00
04407 !
04408 !  Integral to approximate:
04409 !
04410 !    Integral ( -1 <= X <= 1 ) F(X) dX
04411 !
04412 !  Approximate integral:
04413 !
04414 !    Sum ( 1 <= I <= NORDER ) WEIGHT(I) * F ( XTAB(I) )
04415 !
04416 !  Precision:
04417 !
04418 !    The quadrature rule will integrate exactly all polynomials up to
04419 !    X**(2*NORDER-1).
04420 !
04421 !  Note:
04422 !
04423 !    The abscissas of the rule are the zeroes of the Legendre polynomial
04424 !    P(NORDER)(X).
04425 !
04426 !    The integral produced by a Gauss-Legendre rule is equal to the
04427 !    integral of the unique polynomial of degree NORDER-1 which
04428 !    agrees with the function at the NORDER abscissas of the rule.
04429 !
04430 !  Reference:
04431 !
04432 !    Abramowitz and Stegun,
04433 !    Handbook of Mathematical Functions,
04434 !    National Bureau of Standards, 1964.
04435 !
04436 !    Vladimir Krylov,
04437 !    Approximate Calculation of Integrals,
04438 !    MacMillan, 1962.
04439 !
04440 !    Arthur Stroud and Don Secrest,
04441 !    Gaussian Quadrature Formulas,
04442 !    Prentice Hall, 1966.
04443 !
04444 !    Daniel Zwillinger, editor,
04445 !    Standard Mathematical Tables and Formulae,
04446 !    30th Edition,
04447 !    CRC Press, 1996.
04448 !
04449 !  Modified:
04450 !
04451 !    18 December 2000
04452 !
04453 !  Author:
04454 !
04455 !    John Burkardt
04456 !
04457 !  Parameters:
04458 !
04459 !    Input, integer NORDER, the order of the rule.
04460 !    NORDER must be between 1 and 20, 32 or 64.
04461 !
04462 !    Output, double precision XTAB(NORDER), the abscissas of the rule.
04463 !
04464 !    Output, double precision WEIGHT(NORDER), the weights of the rule.
04465 !    The weights are positive, symmetric and should sum to 2.
04466 !
04467   implicit none
04468 !
04469   integer norder
04470 !
04471   double precision xtab(norder)
04472   double precision weight(norder)
04473 !
04474   if ( norder == 1 ) then
04475 
04476     xtab(1) =   0.0D+00
04477 
04478     weight(1) = 2.0D+00
04479

04486     weight(2) = 1.0D+00

04493 
04494     weight(1) = 5.0D+00 / 9.0D+00

04496     weight(3) = 5.0D+00 / 9.0D+00
